Ruling for Amputated Hands and Feet with Facial Wounds
Discusses the ruling for a person with amputated limbs and facial wounds; multiple intra-Hanafi opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the dominant Hanafi ruling for a person with amputated hands and feet and a facial wound, and explain the intra-madhhab differences regarding purification and prayer.

Core Idea
A person with amputated limbs and a facial wound prays without purification—the dominant Hanafi view, despite disagreements.

This passage addresses a challenging scenario: a person who has lost both hands and feet and also has a wound on the face, making both wudu and tayammum impossible. The Hanafi scholars differed on whether such a person must still pray and how. This lesson unpacks the three views and the accepted ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject case
Understand the specific scenario: a person with both hands and feet amputated, and a wound on the face. He cannot perform wudu (no hands/feet) nor tayammum (face wound prevents wiping face). Thus, both forms of purification are impossible.
This is an edge case where normal purification is physically impossible.
2
Recognize the three intra-Hanafi positions
Learn the three views: 1) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: no prayer at all. 2) Abu Yusuf: pray with gestures (īmā') like an imprisoned person. 3) Al-Jami' al-Saghir and others: pray without any purification and do not repeat.
The difference stems from whether purification is a condition or a pillar, and whether necessity overrides.
3
Understand the preponderance (tarjih)
The commentator states the most correct (al-aṣaḥḥ) view is to pray without purification, citing reliable sources like al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Zahiriyya. This becomes the mufta bihi position.
Later authorities favored this view due to the principle of 'necessity permits the forbidden' and the obligation of prayer.
4
Apply to related cases
The text extends: if hands are paralyzed (not amputated), one wipes face and forearms on a wall/ground. If cut above elbow/ankle, washing is dropped entirely, and wiping over khuff of remaining foot is allowed.
This shows the school's consistent approach: when the limb is missing, its purification obligation disappears.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كانَ بوجههِ جِرَاحَةٌ يُصلِّي بغير طهارة، ولا يُعيدُ، وهو الأصح كما في «الجامع الصغير» للكرخي، «والظهيرية»، وغيرهما، وقال بعض المشايخ: سقطت عنه الصلاة بقطع اليدين والرجلين، وقال بعضهم: لا تسقط، وفي «مجموع النوازل»، إن لم يمكنه الوضوء، والتيمم لا يصلي عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وعند أبي يوسف يصلي بالإيماء كالمحبوس ولو شلت يداه، وعجز عن استعمال الطهورين، يمسح وجهه وذراعيه بالحائط أو الأرض، ولا يدع الصلاة، أما على رواية الاكتفاء بأكثر الأعضاء في التيمم فظاهر، وأما على الأخرى فللضرورة، والاحتياط في العبادة، ويفترض غسل ما بقي من عضو الوضوء بعد القطع، وإن قل اعتباراً للجزء بالكل، فكذا في التيمم، لكن في «البزازية» مقطوع المرفق يمسح فيه موضع القطع. انتهى. ولو قطع فوق الكعب والمرفق، سقط الغسل لزوال المحل، ويجوز المسح على خف الباقية لسقوط غسل الأخرى بزوال المحل، فجعلت كالمعدومة من الأصل، فالمسح على الباقية لا يؤدي إلى الجمع بين الأصل والبدل. والله أعلم.
And one who has his hands and feet amputated, and has a wound on his face, prays without purification and does not repeat—that is the most correct view—as in al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Karkhi, al-Zahiriyya, and others. Some scholars said: prayer is dropped from him with the cutting of hands and feet. Some said: it is not dropped. In Majmu' al-Nawazil: If he cannot perform wudu nor tayammum, he does not pray according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf, he prays with gestures (īmā') like an imprisoned person. If his hands are paralyzed and he is unable to use the two purifiers, he wipes his face and forearms on a wall or ground, and does not abandon prayer. As for the narration of being satisfied with the majority of limbs in tayammum, it is apparent; as for the other, due to necessity and precaution in worship. And it is obligatory to wash what remains of the wudu limb after amputation, even if little, considering the part as the whole. So too in tayammum. But in al-Bazzaziyya: one whose elbow is amputated wipes the site of amputation. End. And if the cut is above the ankle and elbow, washing is dropped due to the removal of the site. And it is permitted to wipe over the khuff of the remaining foot because the washing of the other is dropped due to removal of the site, so it is treated as nonexistent from the beginning. Thus wiping over the remaining khuff does not lead to combining the original and the substitute. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person with amputated hands and feet who also has a wound on his face. The base ruling in the matn says: such a person prays without any purification (no wudu, no tayammum) and does not repeat the prayer. The commentator says this is the most correct view, citing al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Zahiriyya, and others. However, there are differences: some earlier scholars (baḍ al-mashāyikh) said that prayer is completely dropped for such a person because he lacks the limbs for purification. Others said it is not dropped. Then, from Majmu' al-Nawazil, we have a three-way ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say such a person does not pray (since purification is impossible and no alternative given). Abu Yusuf says he prays with gestures (īmā') like a person who is imprisoned and cannot perform movements—he makes gestures for the actions of prayer without purification. Then the text discusses a case of paralyzed hands (shullat yadāh): the person wipes his face and forearms on a wall or ground, and does not abandon prayer. This is justified either by the narration that majority of limbs suffice in tayammum, or by necessity and precaution. Then, regarding amputated limbs: it is obligatory to wash what remains of the wudu limb after amputation, even a little, because the part is considered as the whole. Similarly in tayammum, but al-Bazzaziyya says someone with an amputated elbow wipes the site of amputation. If the cut is above the ankle or elbow, the washing is dropped because the 'place' (maḥall) of washing is gone. In that case, it is permitted to wipe over the khuff (leather sock) of the remaining foot, because the washing of the other foot is dropped due to the removal of its site, so it is treated as nonexistent from the beginning. This wiping does not lead to combining the original (water) and substitute (tayammum) because the missing limb is essentially absent.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-īmā'): Gesturing for prayer actions (like bowing and prostrating) when unable to perform them physically.
المسح على الخف (al-masḥ 'alā al-khuff): Wiping over leather socks as a substitute for washing feet in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct (asahh) view, how does a person with amputated hands and feet and a facial wound pray?
A) He does not pray at all
B) He prays with gestures (īmā')
C) He prays without any purification and does not repeat
D) He performs tayammum and then prays

Key Takeaway
The most correct Hanafi position is that a person who cannot perform any purification due to amputations and wounds still prays without purification and does not repeat.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Praying When Unable to Perform Wudu or Tayammum
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer without purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on praying when purification is impossible and identify the disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Purification is a condition for prayer; if impossible, most Hanafis say do not pray, but Abu Yusuf permits prayer with gestures.

This passage from Majmu' al-Nawazil presents a rare intra-Hanafi dispute. When a person cannot perform wudu (due to no water) and cannot perform tayammum (due to inability to use earth), Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad rule that prayer is not performed. Abu Yusuf, however, analogizes to an imprisoned person and allows prayer with gestures (ima). Understanding this difference is crucial for knowing the standard Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the situation: a person cannot perform wudu (no water) and cannot perform tayammum (unable to use earth).
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: he does not pray. Abu Yusuf: he prays with gestures (ima).
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's evidence
He analogizes to an imprisoned person who prays with gestures though unable to purify. This is qiyas.
The imprisoned person case is found in some Hadith or earlier fatwa.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to the majority, no prayer is performed; according to Abu Yusuf, prayer is performed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: do not pray.
This is the standard fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي «مجموع النوازل»، إن لم يمكنه الوضوء، والتيمم لا يصلي عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وعند أبي يوسف يصلي بالإيماء كالمحبوس ولو شلت يداه، وعجز عن استعمال الطهورين، يمسح وجهه وذراعيه بالحائط أو الأرض، ولا يدع الصلاة، أما على رواية الاكتفاء بأكثر الأعضاء في التيمم فظاهر، وأما على الأخرى فللضرورة، والاحتياط في العبادة، ويفترض غسل ما بقي من عضو الوضوء بعد القطع، وإن قل اعتباراً للجزء بالكل، فكذا في التيمم ، لكن في « البزازية» مقطوع المرفق يمسح فيه موضع القطع. انتهى. ولو قطع فوق الكعب والمرفق، سقط الغسل لزوال المحل، ويجوز المسح على خف الباقية لسقوط غسل الأخرى بزوال المحل، فجعلت كالمعدومة من الأصل، فالمسح على الباقية لا يؤدي إلى الجمع بين الأصل والبدل. والله أعلم.
And in 'Majmu' al-Nawazil': If one cannot perform wudu and tayammum, he does not pray according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf, he prays with gestures like the imprisoned person. If both his hands are paralyzed, and he is unable to use the two purifiers, he wipes his face and forearms on the wall or ground, and does not abandon prayer. As for the narration of sufficiency with most limbs in tayammum, it is apparent; as for the other narration, it is due to necessity and precaution in worship. And it is obligatory to wash what remains of the limb of wudu after amputation, even if little, considering the part as the whole. Similarly in tayammum. But in al-Bazzaziyyah: the one amputated at the elbow wipes the place of amputation. End. And if cut above the ankle and elbow, washing is dropped due to removal of the place, and it is permissible to wipe over the remaining khuff because washing the other is dropped due to removal of the place, so it is considered as non-existent from the beginning, so wiping over the remaining does not lead to combining the original and the substitute. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage contains multiple rulings and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The first ruling concerns a person who cannot perform wudu (due to lack of water) and also cannot perform tayammum (due to inability to use earth or being in a situation where tayammum is not possible). According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, such a person does not pray because purification is a condition for prayer and cannot be fulfilled. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, likens this person to one who is imprisoned and unable to find water; such a person prays with gestures (ima) even without purification. The text then addresses a case where both hands are paralyzed and one cannot use either water or earth for purification: the person should wipe his face and forearms on a wall or the ground, and must not abandon prayer. This is based on a narration that in tayammum it suffices to wipe most limbs, or due to the necessity and precaution in worship. Next, the text discusses amputation: if a limb is partially cut, the remaining part must be washed in wudu, using the principle that the part is considered as the whole (juz' bil kull). The same applies in tayammum. However, a specific ruling from al-Bazzaziyyah states that if the amputation is at the elbow, one wipes the place of amputation. Finally, the passage addresses the case of amputation above the ankle or elbow: washing the missing part is no longer required because the place of washing is gone. Consequently, if one leg is amputated above the ankle and the other leg is intact with a khuff, it is permissible to wipe over the remaining khuff because the obligation to wash the amputated leg is dropped, and thus wiping over the one khuff does not combine the original washing with the substitute wiping. This last part transitions to the chapter on wiping over khuffs.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution performed with clean earth or dust when water is unavailable or cannot be used.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head or body in prayer when one is unable to perform the normal postures due to illness or confinement.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precautionary measure in worship to ensure validity and avoid sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what should a person do if they can neither perform wudu nor tayammum?
A) Pray with gestures (ima)
B) Not pray
C) Perform tayammum on the wall
D) Wait until water becomes available then pray

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, if a person cannot perform wudu or tayammum, the relied-upon view is that he does not pray, because purification is an indispensable condition.

Wiping on Wall and Amputation Rulings in Taharah
Rulings for those unable to use normal purification due to paralysis, amputation, or missing limbs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling for a person with paralyzed hands, apply the principle of ihtiyat to tayammum, and state the obligations for amputated limbs and wiping over khuffs when one leg is lost.

Core Idea
Necessity permits wiping on wall; amputation above the joint drops the obligation; partial amputation requires washing the remainder.

This passage continues with practical scenarios where normal purification is impossible. For a person with paralyzed hands who cannot use water or earth, the school allows wiping the face and forearms on a wall or ground, based on either the sufficiency of most limbs in tayammum or the principles of necessity (darurah) and precaution (ihtiyat). Then it addresses amputation: if a limb is partially cut, the remaining part must be washed, applying the principle that the part stands for the whole. But if the cut is above the joint, the obligation drops completely. Furthermore, if one leg is amputated above the ankle, wiping over the remaining khuff is permissible because the obligation on the missing leg is gone, preventing the combination of original and substitute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case of paralyzed hands
A person whose hands are paralyzed cannot use water or earth. The ruling is that he wipes his face and forearms on the wall or ground.
2
Understand the two justifications
One justification is a narration that in tayammum it suffices to wipe most limbs. The other is the general principle of necessity (darurah) and precaution (ihtiyat) in worship.
The two justifications indicate that the ruling is well-grounded.
3
Learn the ruling on partial amputation
If a limb is partially amputated, the remaining part must be washed in wudu (or wiped in tayammum), using the principle that the part is considered as the whole (i'tibar al-juz' bil kull).
4
Distinguish amputation above the joint
If the cut is above the ankle or elbow, the washing is dropped because the place of obligation (mahl) is removed.
5
Apply to wiping over khuffs
If one leg is amputated above the ankle and the other leg has a khuff, it is permissible to wipe over that single khuff. The missing leg is treated as non-existent, so there is no combination of original (washing) and substitute (wiping).
This prevents the prohibited combining of original and substitute.

This last part transitions to the chapter on wiping over khuffs.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution performed with clean earth or dust when water is unavailable or cannot be used.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head or body in prayer when one is unable to perform the normal postures due to illness or confinement.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precautionary measure in worship to ensure validity and avoid sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person whose hands are paralyzed and cannot use water or earth?
A) He does not pray because he cannot purify
B) He wipes his face and forearms on a wall or ground and prays
C) He prays with gestures without any purification
D) He must find someone to assist him

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides practical rulings for those unable to use normal purification: wiping on wall is allowed for the paralyzed, partial amputation requires washing the remainder, and amputation above the joint drops the obligation entirely.

Taharah — Purification

Definition and Legal Nature of Wiping over Khuffs
Defines key terms and legal nature of wiping over khuffs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the terms 'mash' and 'khuff' in Hanafi fiqh and explain the legal nature of wiping over khuffs as a rukhsah.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a temporary license (rukhsah) that lightens the obligation of washing feet in wudu.

This lesson introduces the chapter on wiping over khuffs, explaining why it follows tayammum and what the key terms mean. You will understand the distinction between rukhsah and azimah and how wiping over khuffs is a concession granted by the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the placement of this chapter after tayammum
The author explains that both are purifications by wiping, substitutes for washing, and temporary licenses. Tayammum is placed first because it is established by the Quran, while wiping over khuffs is established by the Sunnah.
This demonstrates the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi fiqh: Quran > Sunnah.
2
Define 'mash' linguistically and technically
Linguistically, it is passing the hand over something. Technically, it is a license limited to one day/night for the resident and three days/nights for the traveler.
The technical definition incorporates the temporal limit.
3
Define 'khuff' and its etymology
In Islamic law, a khuff is leather footwear covering the ankles. It is called khuff from 'khiffah' (lightness) because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping.
The etymology reflects the legal concession.
4
Distinguish between rukhsah and azimah
Azimah is the original strict ruling not based on excuses; rukhsah is a concession based on excuses. Wiping over khuffs is a rukhsah.
This distinction is crucial for understanding why the ruling is sunnah, not fard.
5
State the overall ruling
The author describes wiping over khuffs as a sunnah legislated as a license. In the Hanafi school, it is classified as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah means it is regularly practiced by the Prophet and recommended but not obligatory.

صح المسح على الخُفِّيْنِ، في الحدث الأصغر .
باب المسح على الخفين
إنما أعقب المسح على الخفين التيمم، لأن كل واحد منهما طهارة مسح، أو لأنهما بدلان عن الغسل، أو من حيث أنهما رخصة مؤقتة إلى غاية، وقدم التيمم لثبوته بالكتاب، والمسح على الخفين ثبت بالسنة على الصحيح، قولاً وفعلاً)، كما تقدم، والمسح لغة إمرار اليد على الشيء، واصطلاحاً هنا : عبارة عن رخصة مقدرة بيوم وليلة للمقيم، وثلاثة أيام للمسافر، والخف في الشرع: اسم للمتخذ من الجلد، وما ألحق به الساتر للكعبين، وسمي خفاً من الخفة، لأن الحكم خف به من الغسل إلى المسح ويحتاج إلى بيان سببه، وشرطه، وحكمه، وركنه، وصفته وكيفيته، وبيان مدته وما ينقضه، فسببه لبس الخف، وشرطه كون الخف ساتراً محل الفرض، صالحاً للمسح مع بقاء المدة، وحكمه: حل الصلاة به ونحوها، وركنه مسح القدر المفروض في محله. وصفته: أنه سنة شرعت ترخصاً، لأن العزيمة ما كان أصلياً غير مبني على أعذار العباد، والرخصة: ما بني على أعذار العباد وهو الأصح في تعريفهما وكيفيته ابتداء المسح بأصابع اليدين من رؤوس أصابع الرجل، ومدته يوم وليلة للمقيم، وثلاثة أيام بلياليها للمسافر، وناقضه ناقض الأصل)، ونزع خف ومضي المدة، وستأتيك مبسوطة. (صح)، أي: جاز (المَسْحُ عَلَى الخفين). الصحة في العبادات كونها توجب تفريغ الذمة، فالمعتبر في مفهومها ابتداء، إنما هو المقصود الدنيوي، وهو تفريغ الذمة، وإن كان يلزمها الثواب، وهو المقصود الأخروي، والوجوب في العبادات كون الفعل، بحيث لو أتى به يثاب ولو تركه يعاقب، فالمعتبر في مفهومه اعتباراً ابتدائياً، هو المقصود الأخروي، وإن تبعه المقصود الدنيوي، وهو تفريغ الذمة ( في الحَدَثِ الأصغر)، لما ورد فيه من الأخبار المستفيضة، حتى روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال: ما قلت بالمسح حتى وردت فيه آثـار أضوى من (1) وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا ﴾ [المائدة: ٦ ]. (٢) أما الفعل فحديث المغير له: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وضع يديه على خفيه ومدهما من الأصابع إلى أعلاهما مسحة واحدة، وكأني أنظر إلى أثر المسح على خف رسول الله و خطوطاً بالأصابع. وعن عائشة : ما زال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يمسح على الخفين بعد نزول المائدة حتى قبضه الله تعالى. وأما القول: فما روى علي وجماعة من الصحابة عن النبي : ( يمسح المسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن، والمقيم يوماً وليلة» والأخـبـار فـيـه قـريبـة مـن التواتر. شرح هدية ابن العماد (۳۷۲). (۳) وهو الوضوء.
Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. Wiping over the two khuffs is valid for minor ritual impurity. Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. The wiping over khuffs follows tayammum because each is a purification by wiping, or because they are both substitutes for washing, or because they are temporary licenses with a limit. Tayammum was mentioned first because it is established by the Book (Qur'an), while wiping over khuffs is established by the Sunnah according to the correct view, both by statement and action, as has preceded. Linguistically, 'mash' (wiping) is passing the hand over something. Technically here, it is a license limited to one day and one night for the resident, and three days for the traveler. 'Khuff' in Islamic law is the name for footwear made of leather and what is attached to it that covers the ankles. It is called khuff from 'khiffah' (lightness) because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping. It needs an explanation of its cause, condition, ruling, pillar, description, manner, duration, and what invalidates it. Its cause: wearing the khuff. Its condition: that the khuff covers the place of the obligatory washing, is suitable for wiping, and within the duration. Its ruling: it makes prayer and similar acts permissible with it. Its pillar: wiping the prescribed amount in its place. Its description: it is a sunnah legislated as a license, because 'azimah (strict obligation) is what is original and not based on excuses of the servants, while rukhsah (license) is what is based on excuses of the servants, and this is the more correct definition. Its manner: beginning the wipe with the fingertips from the tips of the toes. Its duration: one day and night for the resident, and three days with their nights for the traveler. Its invalidator: whatever invalidates the original (wudu), removing the khuff, and the passing of the duration. They will come to you in detail. (Sahha) meaning: it is permissible (al-mashu 'ala al-khuffayn). Validity (sihhah) in acts of worship is that they cause the discharge of liability (dhimmah). So the primary consideration in its concept is the worldly objective, which is the discharge of liability, although reward follows as the otherworldly objective. Obligation (wujub) in acts of worship is that if one performs the act he is rewarded, and if he leaves it he is punished. So the primary consideration in its concept is the otherworldly objective, although the worldly objective of discharge of liability follows. (For minor ritual impurity) because of the widely transmitted reports about it, even it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'I did not adopt wiping until reports came to me that were more numerous than...' (1) which is His statement the Exalted: '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum...' [al-Ma'idah:6]. (2) As for the action: the hadith of al-Mughirah: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed his hands on his khuffs and wiped them from the toes to the top with one wipe, and it is as if I see the trace of the wipe on the khuffs of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) as lines from the fingers. And from 'A'ishah: The Prophet (peace be upon him) continued wiping over the khuffs after the revelation of al-Ma'idah until Allah took his soul. As for the statement: what 'Ali and a group of Companions narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The traveler wipes for three days and their nights, and the resident for one day and one night.' And the reports about it are close to tawatur. Explanation from Hadiyyat Ibn al-'Imad (372). (3) i.e., wudu.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs (mash 'ala al-khuffayn). The author first explains why this chapter follows the chapter on tayammum: both are purifications by wiping (taharah mash), both are substitutes for washing (badalan 'an al-ghusl), and both are temporary licenses (rukhsah mu'aqqatah). Tayammum is given precedence because it is established by the Qur'an, while wiping over khuffs is established by the Sunnah according to the correct view. The author then provides linguistic and technical definitions. Linguistically, 'mash' is passing the hand over something. Technically, it is a license limited to one day and night for the resident and three days for the traveler. A 'khuff' in Islamic law is footwear made of leather (or what is attached to it) that covers the ankles. It is called khuff from 'khiffah' (lightness) because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping. The author outlines the components needed: cause (sabab) – wearing the khuff; condition (shart) – the khuff must cover the area of obligation, be suitable for wiping, and within the duration; ruling (hukm) – it permits prayer and similar acts; pillar (rukn) – wiping the required amount in its place; description (sifah) – it is a sunnah legislated as a license; manner (kayfiyyah) – beginning with the fingertips from the toes; duration (muddah) – one day/night for resident, three days/nights for traveler; invalidator (naqid) – anything that invalidates wudu, removing the khuff, or expiry of the duration. The author then clarifies the concept of 'sihhah' (validity) in acts of worship: it is about discharging liability, which is the worldly objective, even though reward is the otherworldly objective. Similarly, 'wujub' (obligation) is primarily about the otherworldly objective (reward/punishment), though it leads to discharge of liability. Wiping over khuffs is proven by the widely transmitted reports, including the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by al-Mughirah and 'A'ishah, and the statement of the Prophet narrated by 'Ali and others specifying the duration. The author notes that the reports are close to tawatur (mass transmission). The footnote clarifies that the Qur'anic verse mentioned (5:6) is about tayammum, not directly about khuffs, but is part of the discussion. Finally, the passage defines the hadath asghar (minor ritual impurity) as the occasion for wiping over khuffs.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): Islamic legal term for footwear made of leather (or similar) that covers the ankles.
المسح (al-mash): Wiping; specifically, passing the wet hand over the khuff or other body part for purification.
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): A legal license that permits an otherwise forbidden act due to necessity or excuse.
العزيمة (al-azimah): The original, strict ruling without any concession; e.g., washing the feet in wudu is azimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the technical definition of 'mash' (wiping) in the context of this chapter?
A) Passing the hand over the khuff with water
B) A license limited to one day/night for the resident and three days/nights for the traveler
C) Washing the khuff with water
D) Removing the khuff and washing the feet

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a sunnah muakkadah and a rukhsah, limited by duration and conditions; it lightens the purity requirement while maintaining legal validity.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Conditions, Pillars, and Invalidators of Wiping over Khuffs
Detailed listing of cause, conditions, pillar, sunnah manner, and invalidators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions, pillar, and invalidators of wiping over khuffs and determine when a wipe is valid or invalid.

Core Idea
The validity of wiping over khuffs depends on covering the ankles, suitability, and duration; its invalidation includes hadath, removal, or expiry.

This lesson focuses on the practical conditions and invalidators of wiping over khuffs as detailed in the chapter. You will learn exactly what is required for the wipe to be valid and what breaks it, enabling you to apply these rules correctly in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause (sabab) of wiping over khuffs
The cause is simply wearing the khuff over the feet while in a state of purity.
This is not a condition but the trigger that makes the ruling applicable.
2
List the conditions (shurut) for validity
Three conditions: (1) the khuff covers the place of obligatory washing (the ankles), (2) the khuff is suitable for wiping (e.g., thick enough to prevent water seeping), (3) the wipe is performed within the permissible duration.
If any condition is missing, the wipe is invalid.
3
Identify the pillar (rukn) of the wipe
The pillar is wiping the prescribed amount on the top of the khuff. This is the essential act that must be performed.
The exact amount: the Hanafi school holds that wiping the front part covering the toes is sufficient, but the sunnah is to wipe from toes to shin.
4
Describe the sunnah manner of wiping
It is sunnah to begin with the fingertips at the toes and wipe upwards, using the right hand for the right foot and left hand for the left foot.
Following the sunnah brings reward; neglecting it does not invalidate.
5
List the invalidators (mufsidat) of wiping
Three invalidators: (1) anything that invalidates wudu (hadath), (2) physically removing the khuff, (3) expiration of the duration (1 day/night for resident, 3 for traveler).
These terminate the license; after any of these, the feet must be washed in subsequent wudu.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an invalidator of wiping over khuffs according to this passage?
A) Removing the khuff
B) Expiry of the duration
C) Minor ritual impurity (hadath)
D) Wiping with dry hands

Key Takeaway
The validity of wiping over khuffs hinges on three conditions (covering, suitability, duration) and is nullified by hadath, removal, or expiry.

Proofs for Wiping over Khuffs from the Sunnah
Cites and explains the prophetic evidence (fi'l and qawl) for wiping over khuffs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the prophetic proofs (fi'l and qawl) for wiping over khuffs and explain why the Hanafi school accepts these reports.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is proven by the Prophet's action (hadith of al-Mughirah and 'A'ishah) and his statement specifying the duration.

This lesson examines the evidential basis for the ruling on wiping over khuffs. The author mentions that the practice is established by the Sunnah through both the Prophet's actions and his words. You will learn the key hadiths and understand their weight according to Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of evidence: action (fi'l) and statement (qawl)
The Prophet's actions establish the permissibility and manner; his words establish the specific duration.
Both are needed: action shows how, statement shows limits.
2
Recount the hadith of al-Mughirah (action)
Al-Mughirah reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed his hands on his khuffs and wiped from the toes to the top with one wipe.
This shows the method of wiping.
3
Recount the hadith of 'A'ishah (continuous practice)
'A'ishah reported that the Prophet continued wiping over khuffs after the revelation of al-Ma'idah until his death, indicating its legitimacy.
This refutes the claim that the practice was abrogated.
4
Recount the hadith of 'Ali (statement on duration)
'Ali and other Companions narrated that the Prophet said: 'The traveler wipes for three days and their nights, and the resident for one day and one night.'
This specifies the temporal limit.
5
Explain the strength of these reports
The author says these reports are 'close to tawatur' (mass transmission), meaning they are very strong. Even Abu Hanifa initially did not accept the practice until he saw these reports.
Hanafi usul accepts ahad hadith with strong chains, but here the multiple transmissions elevate the evidence.

(صح)، أي: جاز (المَسْحُ عَلَى الخفين). الصحة في العبادات كونها توجب تفريغ الذمة، فالمعتبر في مفهومها ابتداء، إنما هو المقصود الدنيوي، وهو تفريغ الذمة، وإن كان يلزمها الثواب، وهو المقصود الأخروي، والوجوب في العبادات كون الفعل، بحيث لو أتى به يثاب ولو تركه يعاقب، فالمعتبر في مفهومه اعتباراً ابتدائياً، هو المقصود الأخروي، وإن تبعه المقصود الدنيوي، وهو تفريغ الذمة ( في الحَدَثِ الأصغر)، لما ورد فيه من الأخبار المستفيضة، حتى روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال: ما قلت بالمسح حتى وردت فيه آثـار أضوى من (1) وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا ﴾ [المائدة: ٦ ]. (۳) وهو الوضوء.
Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. Wiping over the two khuffs is valid for minor ritual impurity. Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. The wiping over khuffs follows tayammum because each is a purification by wiping, or because they are both substitutes for washing, or because they are temporary licenses with a limit. Tayammum was mentioned first because it is established by the Book (Qur'an), while wiping over khuffs is established by the Sunnah according to the correct view, both by statement and action, as has preceded. Linguistically, 'mash' (wiping) is passing the hand over something. Technically here, it is a license limited to one day and one night for the resident, and three days for the traveler. 'Khuff' in Islamic law is the name for footwear made of leather and what is attached to it that covers the ankles. It is called khuff from 'khiffah' (lightness) because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping. It needs an explanation of its cause, condition, ruling, pillar, description, manner, duration, and what invalidates it. Its cause: wearing the khuff. Its condition: that the khuff covers the place of the obligatory washing, is suitable for wiping, and within the duration. Its ruling: it makes prayer and similar acts permissible with it. Its pillar: wiping the prescribed amount in its place. Its description: it is a sunnah legislated as a license, because 'azimah (strict obligation) is what is original and not based on excuses of the servants, while rukhsah (license) is what is based on excuses of the servants, and this is the more correct definition. Its manner: beginning the wipe with the fingertips from the tips of the toes. Its duration: one day and night for the resident, and three days with their nights for the traveler. Its invalidator: whatever invalidates the original (wudu), removing the khuff, and the passing of the duration. They will come to you in detail. (Sahha) meaning: it is permissible (al-mashu 'ala al-khuffayn). Validity (sihhah) in acts of worship is that they cause the discharge of liability (dhimmah). So the primary consideration in its concept is the worldly objective, which is the discharge of liability, although reward follows as the otherworldly objective. Obligation (wujub) in acts of worship is that if one performs the act he is rewarded, and if he leaves it he is punished. So the primary consideration in its concept is the otherworldly objective, although the worldly objective of discharge of liability follows. (For minor ritual impurity) because of the widely transmitted reports about it, even it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'I did not adopt wiping until reports came to me that were more numerous than...' (1) which is His statement the Exalted: '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum...' [al-Ma'idah:6]. (2) As for the action: the hadith of al-Mughirah: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed his hands on his khuffs and wiped them from the toes to the top with one wipe, and it is as if I see the trace of the wipe on the khuffs of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) as lines from the fingers. And from 'A'ishah: The Prophet (peace be upon him) continued wiping over the khuffs after the revelation of al-Ma'idah until Allah took his soul. As for the statement: what 'Ali and a group of Companions narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The traveler wipes for three days and their nights, and the resident for one day and one night.' And the reports about it are close to tawatur. Explanation from Hadiyyat Ibn al-'Imad (372). (3) i.e., wudu.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs (mash 'ala al-khuffayn). The author first explains why this chapter follows the chapter on tayammum: both are purifications by wiping (taharah mash), both are substitutes for washing (badalan 'an al-ghusl), and both are temporary licenses (rukhsah mu'aqqatah). Tayammum is given precedence because it is established by the Qur'an, while wiping over khuffs is established by the Sunnah according to the correct view. The author then provides linguistic and technical definitions. Linguistically, 'mash' is passing the hand over something. Technically, it is a license limited to one day and night for the resident and three days for the traveler. A 'khuff' in Islamic law is footwear made of leather (or what is attached to it) that covers the ankles. It is called khuff from 'khiffah' (lightness) because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping. The author outlines the components needed: cause (sabab) – wearing the khuff; condition (shart) – the khuff must cover the area of obligation, be suitable for wiping, and within the duration; ruling (hukm) – it permits prayer and similar acts; pillar (rukn) – wiping the required amount in its place; description (sifah) – it is a sunnah legislated as a license; manner (kayfiyyah) – beginning with the fingertips from the toes; duration (muddah) – one day/night for resident, three days/nights for traveler; invalidator (naqid) – anything that invalidates wudu, removing the khuff, or expiry of the duration. The author then clarifies the concept of 'sihhah' (validity) in acts of worship: it is about discharging liability, which is the worldly objective, even though reward is the otherworldly objective. Similarly, 'wujub' (obligation) is primarily about the otherworldly objective (reward/punishment), though it leads to discharge of liability. Wiping over khuffs is proven by the widely transmitted reports, including the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by al-Mughirah and 'A'ishah, and the statement of the Prophet narrated by 'Ali and others specifying the duration. The author notes that the reports are close to tawatur (mass transmission). The footnote clarifies that the Qur'anic verse mentioned (5:6) is about tayammum, not directly about khuffs, but is part of the discussion. Finally, the passage defines the hadath asghar (minor ritual impurity) as the occasion for wiping over khuffs.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): Islamic legal term for footwear made of leather (or similar) that covers the ankles.
المسح (al-mash): Wiping; specifically, passing the wet hand over the khuff or other body part for purification.
الفعل (al-fi'l): Action of the Prophet; a source of legislation.
القول (al-qawl): Statement of the Prophet; a source of legislation.
التواتر (al-tawatur): Mass transmission; a hadith narrated by many chains that makes it indisputable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Abu Hanifa say about wiping over khuffs?
A) He rejected it because it is not in the Quran.
B) He did not adopt it until reports came to him.
C) He considered it wajib.
D) He said it was only for travelers.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is firmly established by the Prophet's action and statement, making it a validated sunnah practice.

Ruling and Evidence for Wiping over Khuffayn
Defines wiping over khuff and provides evidence from Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuff, identify the Sunnah evidence for its validity, and explain the conditions, duration, and nullifiers of this concession.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuff is a valid, time-limited concession proven by widely transmitted Sunnah.

This lesson examines the ruling of wiping over leather socks (khuffayn) in the Hanafi school. The passage clarifies that while tayammum is proven by the Quran, wiping over khuff is established by the Prophet's sayings and actions, which are nearly mutawatir. We will explore the legal definition, conditions, how to perform it, and what invalidates it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states 'sahha al-masḥu ʿalā al-khuffayn' – wiping over khuff is valid (sahih) for purification from minor hadath. Note that it is a rukhsa (concession), not the ʿazīmah (original resolution).
Wiping substitutes washing of the feet in wudu.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Sunnah: the hadith of al-Mughīrah (action), ʿĀ’ishah (continuity after revelation of al-Mā’idah), and ʿAlī (saying) narrating the duration. The reports are described as 'mustafīḍah' and near tawātur.
Imam Abū Ḥanīfah said he only accepted wiping after reports 'brighter than the sun'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The explicit words and actions of the Prophet prescribe a specific duration (one day/night for resident, three for traveler) and demonstrate the manner of wiping. This establishes both validity and the limits of the concession.
4
Summarize conditions, duration, and nullifiers
From the text: cause = wearing the khuff; condition = covering the obligatory area and suitability; pillar = wiping the prescribed amount; duration = 1 day/night for resident, 3 for traveler; nullifiers = anything that nullifies wudu, removal of khuff, or expiry of time.
Details are expanded later in the commentary.

Chapter on wiping over the two khuffs. Wiping over the two khuffs is valid for minor hadath. This chapter follows tayammum because both are purifications by wiping, or because they are substitutes for washing, or because they are time-limited concessions. Tayammum was placed first due to its proof from the Book, while wiping over khuff is proven by the Sunnah, as per the correct view, in both word and deed, as has preceded. Linguistically, wiping (al-mash) means passing the hand over something; terminologically here it is a concession limited to one day and night for the resident and three days for the traveler. Legally, khuff is a name for something made of leather or what is attached to it, covering the ankles. It is named khuff from lightness (al-khiffah), because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping. It requires explanation of its cause, condition, ruling, pillar, description, manner, period, and nullifiers. Its cause is wearing the khuff. Its condition is that the khuff covers the obligatory area, is suitable for wiping for the duration. Its ruling is the permissibility of prayer and similar acts with it. Its pillar is wiping the prescribed amount in its place. Its description is that it is a sunnah legislated as a concession, because 'azimah is what is original not based on excuses, while rukhṣah is based on excuses; this is the soundest definition of the two. Its manner is beginning the wipe with the fingertips of the hands from the tips of the toes. Its period is one day and night for the resident and three days with their nights for the traveler. Its nullifiers are what nullifies the original (wudu) and removal of the khuff and passage of the period. Details will come later. (The word 'sah' means) it is valid (wiping over the two khuffs). Validity in acts of worship is that they cause discharge of liability; the primary consideration in its concept is worldly objective—discharge of liability, even though reward follows, which is the otherworldly objective. Obligation in acts of worship is that the act is such that if one performs it he is rewarded, and if he leaves it he is punished; the primary consideration in its concept is the otherworldly objective, even if the worldly objective follows. (In minor hadath), due to the widely transmitted reports that have come, to the extent that it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: I did not speak about wiping until reports came to me brighter than the sun, to the point that he said: Whoever denies wiping over khuff is to be feared for his disbelief. End. (1) And it is His saying: {and if you do not find water, then perform tayammum}. (2) As for the action, it is the hadith of al-Mughirah: that the Prophet placed his hands on his khuffs and drew them from the fingers to the top in one wipe, and as if I am looking at the trace of wiping on the Khuff of the Messenger of Allah as lines by fingers. And from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah continued to wipe over the two khuffs after the revelation of al-Ma'idah until Allah took his soul. As for the saying, it is what Ali and a group of companions narrated from the Prophet: The traveler wipes three days and their nights, and the resident one day and a night. And the reports on it are near tawatur. (3) And it means the minor hadath (wudu).

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on wiping over leather socks (khuffayn). The author first explains the order of placement after tayammum, noting that both are forms of purification by wiping and both are concessions. He then provides linguistic and technical definitions of masah and khuff. The ruling is that wiping over khuff is valid for minor hadath only, not for major impurity. The proof is from the widely transmitted Sunnah, both in word and deed, citing specific hadiths. The passage also outlines the key elements: cause (wearing khuff), condition (covering the obligatory area), ruling (permissibility of prayer), pillar (wiping the prescribed amount), description (it is a sunnah concession), manner (starting from toes), duration (one day/night for resident, three for traveler), and nullifiers (anything that nullifies wudu, removal, or expiration of period). The commentary emphasizes that the reports are so strong that Imam Abu Hanifa considered denial a serious matter.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A leather covering for the foot that covers the ankles, or any thick material that serves the same purpose.
المسح (al-masḥ): Passing a wet hand over the khuff in a prescribed manner as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
الحدث الأصغر (al-ḥadath al-aṣghar): Minor state of impurity that requires wudu, such as passing wind, urine, or sleep.

Permissibility for Men and Women and Material of Khuff
Expands the ruling on khuff: gender and material

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid wiping on non-leather khuffs and explain why the Hanafi ruling applies to both genders.

Core Idea
Wiping on khuff is valid for both genders and on any thick material that stays on the leg and blocks water.

This passage expands the scope of wiping over khuff beyond the common leather type. It confirms that the ruling includes both men and women, and it establishes that thick non-leather materials (like felt or thick cotton) are valid substitutes as long as they meet certain conditions. The text also traces an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf that was resolved in favor of broader permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and overall ruling
The act is wiping over khuff (masḥ ‘alā al-khuffayn) during wudu. The ruling: permissible (mubāḥ) for both men and women, whether traveling or residing, for need or otherwise.
2
Analyze the material conditions
The khuff may be made of any thick material (takhīn) that is not leather, provided it stays on the leg without tying and does not allow water to seep through when wiped. Examples given: felt (libad), coarse cloth (jūkh), thick cotton (karbās).
Condition: the material must be impermeable and self‑supporting.
3
Understand the gender inclusiveness
The ruling applies equally to men and women because the general texts (iṭlāq al-nuṣūṣ) do not specify one gender; legal address to one includes the other unless explicitly restricted.
This is a Hanafi usul principle: khitāb wārid li-aḥadihimā yashmil al-ākhar illā bi takhṣīṣ.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and its resolution
Abu Hanifa initially disallowed wiping on non-leather khuffs, but he later reverted to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, who allowed it. The muftā bihī (relied-upon) position is permissibility, even if the khuff has no leather at all.
The text openly records the school's internal development and the final tarjīḥ.

Source Text

للرجال والنساء) سفراً وحضراً لحاجة ولغيرها؛ لإطلاق النصوص؛ ولأن الخطاب الوارد لأحدهما يكون وارداً في حق الآخر، ما لم ينص على التخصيص، (ولو كانا) أي: الخفين، متخذين (من شيء تخين، غير الجلد) كلبد وجوخ وكرباس ثخين، يستمسك على الساق من غير شد، ولا يشف الماء بالمسح، وجواز المسح عليه هو المفتى به، وهو قولهما، وإليه رجع الإمام رحمه الله، لأنه في معنى الخف المتخذ من الجلد، (سواء كان لهما نعل من جلد)، ويقال له: جورب منعل، وهو الذي وضع على أسفله جلدة كالنعل للقدم، ويقال: أنعل الخف ونعله، جعل له نعلاً، وإذا جعل أعلاه وأسفله، يقال له: مجلداً (أو لا) أي: أو لم يكن فيهما جلد أصلاً على المفتى به، كما ذكرناه
(For men and women) whether traveling or residing, whether for need or otherwise, due to the generality of the texts, and because the address to one includes the other unless specified otherwise. (Even if the two khuffs are) taken from something thick, non-leather, like felt, coarse cloth, and thick cotton, that stay on the leg without tying and do not let water seep through when wiping. The permissibility of wiping on them is the muftā bihī (relied-upon) position, and it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the Imam (Abu Hanifa) reverted to it, because it is like the khuff made of leather. (Whether they have a leather sole) and it is called a soled sock (jūrab mun‘al), which has a leather piece on its bottom like a sole for the foot. It is said: he soled the khuff and its nā‘il, i.e., he made a sole for it. If its upper and lower are both leather, it is called mujallad. (Or not) meaning: or there is no leather in them at all according to the muftā bihī, as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling that wiping over khuff applies to both men and women, based on the generality of the texts. It also addresses the material of the khuff, ruling that even if the khuff is made of thick non-leather materials such as felt (libad), coarse cloth (jūkh), or thick cotton (karbās), wiping on them is permissible. This is the relied-upon (muftā bihī) position, and it is the view of the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); Imam Abu Hanifa later reverted to their opinion. The condition is that the material must be thick enough to stay on the leg without tying and not allow water to seep through. Furthermore, it does not matter whether the khuff has a leather sole or not—both are permissible according to the muftā bihī. The passage thus clarifies the scope of the ruling beyond the common leather khuff.

Key Terms
تخين (thakhīn): Thick material that can serve as a khuff substitute, such as felt, coarse cloth, or thick cotton.
جورب منعل (jūrab mun‘al): A sock that has a leather piece on its sole, considered a type of khuff.
مجلد (mujallad): A khuff that is entirely made of leather, both upper and sole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on wiping over a khuff made of thick cotton without any leather?
A) Invalid, because it must be leather
B) Permissible, as it is the muftā bihī position
C) Permissible only if it has a leather sole
D) Disliked (makruh) but valid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits wiping over khuff for both genders and on any thick, self-supporting, impermeable material, even without leather, based on the final consensus of the three imams.

First Condition for Wiping and Invalidity for Major Impurity
Details the first condition and the invalidity for major impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for wiping over khuff and explain why wiping is invalid for a person in major impurity (junub), citing the hadith of Safwan.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuff requires they be worn after washing the feet; and it is never valid for major impurity.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes two foundational rulings for the permissibility of wiping over khuffs (leather socks). First, the timing of wearing them matters—they must be put on after the feet are washed, even if wudu is not yet complete, as long as it finishes before a nullifier. Second, the concession of wiping does not extend to states of major impurity (janabah, nifas, and by extension menstruation). The proof is a clear hadith from Safwan ibn ‘Assāl, which makes an explicit exception for janabah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
The first of seven conditions is that the khuff must be worn after washing both feet clean. This ensures the feet are in a state of purity when the khuff is put on.
Even if wudu is not yet fully complete, the condition is satisfied as long as wudu is completed before anything nullifies it.
2
Understand the ruling for major impurity
The passage states that wiping is not valid for a junub (person in major impurity) or a nufasā' (postpartum woman) upon purification. This is because the concession of wiping is for minor, recurrent impurities, not for major ones which are non-recurrent.
Abu Yusuf extends this to menstruation based on his view that the minimum haid is two days.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The hadith of Safwan ibn ‘Assāl reports the Prophet's command not to remove khuffs for three days except in the case of janabah. This explicit exception proves that janabah nullifies the concession.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in the Hanafi school and others.
4
Note the better practice
Even when wiping is permissible, performing the azimah (original resolution, i.e., washing the feet) is more rewarding and still valid.
Choosing the harder but complete act brings more reward.
5
Apply the illustration from al-Kafi
If a person becomes junub after wearing khuffs, he must remove them to wash his feet; he may not simply wipe over them.
This illustration removes any doubt about the ruling's rigor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لجواز المسح على الخفين سبعة شرائط الأول: لبسهما بعد غسل الرجلين، ولو قبل كمال الوضوء، إذا أتمه قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء. الشمس، حتى قال: من أنكر المسح على الخفين يخاف عليه الكفر. انتهى. وإذا اعتقد جوازه، ولكنه يأتي بالعزيمة، كان أولى؛ لأنه أشق فيثاب، ولا يصح المسح على الخف للجنب والنفساء إذا طهرت، لأن النفاس لا حد لأقله، فيوجد بعد لبس الخف على طهر، ثم ينقضي قبل انتهاء مدة لبس الخف، ويتصور في الحائض على قول أبي يوسف، بأن أقل الحيض يومان وليلتان، وأكثر الثالث؛ لحديث صفوان بن عسال بالمهملتين أنه قال: «كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يأمرنا إذا كنا سفراً أن لا ننزع خفافنا ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن، إلا من جنابة، لا من غائط أو بول أو نوم»، ولأن الرخصة للحرج فيما يتكرر، ولا حرج في الجنابة ونحوها لعدم التكرار، والتحقيق أنه لا يحتاج لتصوير منع المسح على الخف في الجنابة ونحوها، لأن المقام مقام النفي، وصوره في (الكافي) تقريباً للمتعلم، بأنه توضأ ولبس جوربين مجلدين ثم أجنب، ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعاً، يعني: أو ماداً رجليه على شيء مرتفع ويمسح عليه. انتهى.
And there are seven conditions for the permissibility of wiping over the two khuffs. The first: wearing them after washing the feet, even if before completing the wudu, if he completes it before occurrence of a nullifier of wudu. The sun, even to the point that he said: 'Whoever denies wiping over the two khuffs is to be feared for his disbelief.' End. And if he believes in its permissibility but performs the original resolution, it is better, because it is more arduous and thus more rewarded. And wiping over the khuff is not valid for the junub (person in major impurity) nor for the nufasā' (postpartum woman) after she becomes pure, because nifās has no minimum limit, so it could occur after wearing the khuff while in a state of purity, then end before expiry of the period of wearing the khuff. And it can be imagined for the menstruating woman according to the view of Abu Yusuf, because the minimum of menstruation is two days and two nights, and its maximum is ten. Based on the hadith of Safwan ibn ‘Assāl: 'The Prophet commanded us when we were traveling not to remove our khuffs for three days and their nights except for janābah, not from defecation, urine, or sleep.' And because the concession (rukhsa) is for hardship in repeated matters, and there is no hardship in janābah and the like due to non-repetition. The reality is that there is no need to illustrate the prevention of wiping on the khuff for janābah, because the context is negation. But al-Kāfī illustrated it for the student's approximation: he performed wudu, wore two mujallad socks, then became junub; he may not tighten them and wash the rest of his body lying down, meaning or extending his legs on something elevated and wiping over them. End.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage addresses two distinct rulings. First, it lists the first of seven conditions for valid wiping: the khuff must be worn after the feet are washed (even if before completing the rest of wudu, provided wudu is completed before any nullifier occurs). This ensures the feet are in a state of purity when the khuff is put on. Second, it states that wiping is absolutely invalid for those in major impurity (junub, nifas, and by extension menstruation according to Abu Yusuf). The proof is the hadith of Safwan ibn ‘Assāl, which explicitly excludes janābah from the concession of wiping, while minor impurities like defecation, urine, and sleep do not prevent it. The rationale is that the concession is for recurrent hardships, but major impurity is not recurrent. The passage also notes that performing ‘azimah (complete washing) despite the concession is better and more rewarding. Finally, it cites a practical illustration from al-Kāfī: if a person becomes junub after wearing khuffs, they must remove them to wash their feet.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (full body wash) due to sexual activity or discharge.
النفساء (al-nufasā'): A woman in the postpartum period of bleeding; wiping is invalid for her similar to janabah.
شرط (sharṭ): A condition prerequisite for the validity of wiping. The first condition is wearing the khuff after washing the feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first condition for the validity of wiping over khuff?
A) Wearing the khuff after wudu is completed.
B) Wearing the khuff after washing the feet.
C) Wearing the khuff before any impurity occurs.
D) Wearing leather khuffs only.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuff requires wearing them after washed feet and is never valid for major impurity, as proven by the hadith of Safwan.

Taharah — Purification

First Four Conditions for Wiping Over Khuffs
Explaining conditions 1-4 for wiping over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first four conditions for valid wiping over khuffs and apply the Hanafi principle that the khuff is a preventer (mani‘) not a remover (rafi‘).

Core Idea
Khuffs prevent hadath from reaching the foot; conditions ensure they serve this purpose.

Wiping over khuffs is a well-known concession in wudu, but it is not unconditional. The Hanafi school specifies seven conditions for its validity. This lesson covers the first four: wearing after washing the feet, covering the ankles, possibility of continuous walking, and freedom from large holes. Understanding these conditions clarifies why the khuff is a preventer of impurity transmission, not a remover, and why certain materials and states are acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition and its rationale
Read the first condition: wearing khuffs after washing the feet, even if before completing wudu, provided wudu is finished before any nullifier. Understand that the khuff is a preventer (mani‘), so purity before wearing is critical.
The khuff does not remove hadath; it prevents its transmission.
2
Analyze the second and third conditions
Second condition: khuffs must cover the ankles from the sides (visibility from top is excused). Third condition: continuous walking must be possible—khuffs of glass, wood, or iron are invalid. Note the underlying purpose of ease in travel.
Covering requirement is from sides; walking feasibility is essential for the concession.
3
Examine the fourth condition regarding holes
Fourth condition: no hole equal to three smallest toes of the foot. Relied-upon view: measure by toes, not fingers, and by istihsan small holes are excused. Distinguish between open and closed holes.
Larger holes defeat the purpose of covering; small holes are customary.
4
Connect to the broader Hanafi position
Note that the permissibility of non-leather khuffs (thick felt, cotton) is the mufta bihi view, to which Imam Abu Hanifa reverted. This shows evolution within the school and reliance on istihsan.
The proof is the hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal, which is zanni in transmission and meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للرجال والنساء، ولو كانا من شيء تخين، غير الجلد سواء كان لهما نعل من جلد، أو لا. وَيُشْتَرَطُ لِجَوَازِ المَسْحِ على الخُفِّيْنِ سَبْعَةُ شَرَائِطِ الأَولُ: لُبْسُهُمَا بعدَ غَسْلِ الرّجلين، ولو قَبل كمال الوضوء، إذا أَتَمَّهُ قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء. الشمس، حتى قال: من أنكر المسح على الخفين يخاف عليه الكفر. انتهى. وإذا اعتقد جوازه، ولكنه يأتي بالعزيمة، كان أولى؛ لأنه أشق فيثاب، ولا يصح المسح على الخف للجنب والنفساء إذا طهرت، لأن النفاس لا حد لأقله، فيوجد بعد لبس الخف على طهر ، ثم ينقضي قبل انتهاء مدة لبس الخف، ويتصور في الحائض على قول أبي يوسف، بأن أقل الحيض يومان وليلتان، وأكثر الثالث؛ لحديث صفوان بن عسال بالمهملتين أنه قال: « كانَ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يأمرنا إذا كُنَّا سَفَراً أَنْ لَا تَنزِعَ خفافنَا ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن، إلأ من جنابة، لا من غائط أو بول أو نوم ، ولأن الرخصة للحرج فيما يتكرر، ولا حرج في الجنابة ونحوها لعدم التكرار، والتحقيق أنه لا يحتاج لتصوير منع المسح على الخف في الجنابة ونحوها، لأن المقام مقام النفي، وصوره في ( الكافي» تقريباً للمتعلم، بأنه توضـاً ولبس جوربين مجلدين ثم أجنب، ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعاً، يعني: أو ماداً رجليه على شيء مرتفع ويمسح عليه. انتهى. (للرِّجَالِ والنِّسَاءِ) سفراً وحـضـراً لحاجة ولغيرهـا؛ لإطلاق النصوص؛ ولأن الخطاب الوارد لأحدهما يكون وارداً في حق الآخر، مـا لـم يـنـص عـلـى التخصيص، (وَلَوْ كَانَـا ) أي : الخفين، متخذين ( من شيءٍ نَخِين، غيرِ الجلدِ) كلبد (٣) و وجوخ وكرباس (۳) ثخين، يستمسك على الساق من غير شد، ولا يشف الماء بالمسح، وجواز المسح عليه هو المفتى به، وهو قولهما، وإليه رجع الإمام رحمه الله، لأنه في معنى الخف المتخذ من الجلد، (سَوَاءٌ كَانَ لَهُمَا نَعْلٌ مِنْ جِلْدٍ)، ويقال له: جورب منعل، وهو الذي وضع على أسفله جلدة كالنعل للقدم، ويقال: أنعل الخف ونعله، جعل له نعلاً، وإذا جعل أعلاه وأسفله، يقال له: مجلداً (أو لا ) أي: أو لم يكن فيهما جلد أصلاً على المفتى به، كما ذكرناه (وَيُشْتَرَطُ لِجَوَازِ المَسْحِ عَلَى الخُفَّينِ سَبْعَةُ شَرَائِطَ الأوّلُ) منها: (لُبْسُهُمَا بعد غسل الرجلين)، ولو حكماً، كما لو مسح على جبائر برجليه أو بإحداهما، وغسل الأخرى ثم لبس خفيه فإنه يمسح على خفيه ما دام العذر موجوداً في المدة، لأن مسح الجبيرة كالغسل، (وَلَو ) كان اللبس (قبل كمال الوضوء، إذا أَتَمـه)، أي: الوضوء (قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء)؛ لأن الخف مانع سراية الحدث بالقدم لا رافع، فإذا تمت الطهارة قبل حصول ناقض، ارتفع الحدث عن أعضاء الوضوء بمجموع الغسلين الأول الذي قبل لبس الخف، والثاني: بعد لبسه، فكان الخف مانعاً لا رافعاً، والترتيب في الوضوء ليس شرطاً عندنا، كما تقدم، فيصح المسح عليه. إذا أحدث بعده، واحترزنا باشتراط إتمام الوضوء عن وضوء غير مسبغ، فإنه إذا أحدث قبل الاستيعاب، لا يجوز له المسح على الخف أصلاً. وأما أصحاب الأعذار، إذا توضؤوا مع العذر، أو وجد بعد تمام الوضوء قبل لبس الخف، فإنهم يمسحون ما دام الوقـت بـاقـيـاً. والمتيمم إذا لبس خفيه ثم وجد الماء، لا يمسح لعدم كمال طهارة المعذورين، لأن وضوء المعذور يبطل بخروج الوقت لظهور الحدث السابق، ووضوء المتيمم، وإن كان طهارة كاملة يبطل لظهور الحدث السابق أيضاً بوجود الماء، فلو جاز لهم المسح بعد ذلك، لكان الخف رافعاً للحدث، لا مانعاً. وأما إذا توضأ المعذور ولبس قبل طرو عذره، فإنه يمسح كالأصحاء إلى تمـام المـدة. (وَ) الشرط (الثاني: سَتْرُهُما )، أي: الخفين (للكَعْبَينِ) من الجوانب فلا يضر نظر الكعبين من أعلى خف قصير الساق، لضرورة وسعه للبس، والذي لا يغطي الكعبين، إذا خيط به ثخين كجوخ يصح المسح عليه، (و) الشرط (الثالث: إمكانُ متابعة المشي فيهما، أي الخفين لأن الرخصة شرعت لأجل متابعة فـ المشي، فينعدم بانعدامها، (فلا يَجُوزُ ) المسح ( عَلَى حُفْ) متخذ (منْ زُجَاجِ، أَوْ خَشَبٍ، أَوْ حَدِيدٍ) أن الرخصة إنما شرعت لأجل متابعة المشي في الخف للضرورة، ولا يمكن متابعة المشي في الخف المتخذ . هذه الأشياء بغير اعتماد على غيره. (و) الشرط (الرَّابع: خُلُو كلِّ من منهما)، أي: الخفين (عَنْ حَرْقٍ قَدْرَ ثلاث أصابع من أصغَرِ أصابع القدم)، لأنـه محـل الـمشـي، وقيل: يعتبر بأصابع اليد، فلا يمنع ما دون ذلك، استحساناً، لأن الخفاف لا تخلو عن قليــل الخــرق عادة، والشرع علق المسح بمسمى الخف، وهو الساتر المخصوص الذي يقطع به المسافة، وما كان كذلك فهذا المعنى موجود فيه، والاسم مطلقاً يطلق عليه، بخلاف الخف المشتمل على الكثير، فإن هذا المعنى معدوم فيه، والحرج يوجد بمنع القليل من الخروق، لا الكثير، وفي اعتبار الأصابع مضمومة أو مفرجة اختلاف المشايخ و محل اعتباره بأصغر الأصابع إذا انكشف غير الأصابع، وأما إذا انكشفت الأصابع تعتبر بنفسها، فلا يمنع انكشاف الكبير مع جاره، وإن بلغ قدر ثلاث هي أصغرها على الأصح. والخرق المانع هو: المنفرج الذي يرى ما تحته، أو يكون منضمـاً لـكـن لما قلناه من
For men and women, even if they (the khuffs) are made of thick material other than leather, whether or not they have a leather sole. Seven conditions are required for the permissibility of wiping over the khuffs. The first: wearing them after washing the feet, even if before completing wudu, provided he completes it before occurrence of a nullifier of wudu. ... The sun, so that he said: Whoever denies wiping over the khuffs fears disbelief for him. End. And if he believes its permissibility, but he performs the resolve, it is better because it is more difficult and rewardable. Wiping over the khuff is not valid for a junub or a woman with postpartum bleeding when she becomes pure, because postpartum bleeding has no minimum limit; so it occurs after wearing the khuff while in a state of purity, then it ends before the expiration of the duration of wearing the khuff, and it is conceivable for a menstruating woman according to the saying of Abu Yusuf, that the minimum of menstruation is two days and two nights, and the maximum is three; due to the hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal that he said: 'The Prophet ﷺ used to command us when we were traveling not to remove our khuffs for three days and nights except from janabah, not from defecation, urine, or sleep.' And because the concession is for hardship in what is repetitive, and there is no hardship in janabah and similar because of lack of repetition. And the reality is that there is no need to depict forbidding wiping over the khuff in janabah and similar, because the context is negation. And he depicted it in al-Kafi as an approximation for the learner: that he performed wudu and wore two leather-lined socks then became junub; he may not tighten them and wash the rest of his body while lying down, meaning stretching his legs on something high, and wipe over them. End. (For men and women) traveling and at home, for need and otherwise; due to the absoluteness of texts; and because the address coming to one of them comes with respect to the other, unless specification is stated. (And even if they are) i.e., the khuffs, taken (from something thick, not leather) like felt and broadcloth and thick cotton, which hold on the leg without tying, and do not let water seep through when wiping. The permissibility of wiping on them is the mufta bihi (relied upon) view, and it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Imam (Abu Hanifa) reverted to it, may Allah have mercy on him, because it is in the meaning of a khuff made of leather. (Whether they have a leather sole) and it is called a soled sock, which is one with a piece of leather placed on its bottom like a sole for the foot; and it is said: 'he soled the khuff,' i.e., attached a sole to it. And if its upper and lower parts are made of leather, it is called 'mujallad' (fully leather). (Or not) i.e., they have no leather at all according to the mufta bihi view, as we mentioned. (And seven conditions are required for the permissibility of wiping over the khuffs: the first) of them: (wearing them after washing the feet) even if in a virtual sense, as if he wiped over bandages on his feet or one of them and washed the other then wore his khuffs, he may wipe over his khuffs as long as the excuse exists within the period, because wiping over the bandage is like washing. (And even if) the wearing (was before completing wudu, provided he completes it) i.e., the wudu (before occurrence of a nullifier of wudu); because the khuff is a preventer of the transmission of hadath from the foot, not a remover. So when purity is achieved before a nullifier occurs, hadath is removed from the wudu limbs by the combination of the first washing (before wearing the khuff) and the second (after wearing it); thus the khuff is a preventer, not a remover. And order in wudu is not a condition according to us, as previously mentioned; so wiping over it is valid if he then has an event. And we restricted by the condition of completing wudu to wudu that is not incomplete; because if he had an event before completion, he may not wipe over the khuff at all. As for those with excuses, if they performed wudu with the excuse, or the excuse occurred after completing wudu before wearing the khuff, they may wipe as long as the time remains. And the mutayammim if he wore his khuffs then found water, he may not wipe because the purity of those with excuses is not complete; because the wudu of one with an excuse is invalidated by the exit of time due to appearance of the previous hadath, and the wudu of the mutayammim, even though it is a complete purity, is invalidated by the appearance of the previous hadath also by finding water. So if wiping were permitted for them after that, the khuff would be a remover of hadath, not a preventer. And if one with an excuse performed wudu and wore (the khuffs) before the occurrence of his excuse, he may wipe like healthy persons until the end of the period. (And) the (second condition: covering) i.e., the khuffs (of the ankles) from the sides, so it does not matter if the ankles are visible from the top of a short-legged khuff, due to the necessity of its width for wearing. And what does not cover the ankles, if thick material like broadcloth is sewn to it, wiping is valid. (And) the (third condition: possibility of continuous walking in them), i.e., the khuffs, because the concession was legislated for continuous walking, so it is absent when that is absent. (So it is not permissible) to wipe (on a khuff made of glass, or wood, or iron) because the concession was only legislated for continuous walking in the khuff out of necessity, and continuous walking in a khuff made of these things is not possible without reliance on something else. (And) the (fourth condition: each of them being free) i.e., the khuffs (from a hole equal to three fingers of the smallest toes of the foot) because it is the place of walking. And it is said: it is measured by the fingers of the hand, so what is less than that does not prevent, by istihsan, because khuffs are not usually free from small holes, and the law attached wiping to the name of khuff, which is the specific covering with which distance is traversed, and when it is like that, this meaning is present in it, and the name is absolutely applied to it, unlike the khuff containing many (holes), for this meaning is absent in it, and hardship would be caused by forbidding small holes, not large ones. And regarding whether the fingers are considered together or spread apart, there is disagreement among the scholars. And the place of its consideration is the smallest finger when what is exposed is other than the fingers; but if the fingers themselves are exposed, they are considered by themselves, so exposure of the big toe together with its neighbor does not prevent, even if it reaches the measure of three, if it is the smallest, on the soundest view. And the hole that prevents is the one that is open, revealing what is beneath, or is closed but... for what we have said.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah explains the first four of the seven conditions required for the validity of wiping over khuffs during wudu. The author begins by affirming that the dispensation of wiping over khuffs applies to both men and women, in travel or residence, regardless of need. The khuffs may be made of any thick material like felt (libd), broadcloth (jukh), or thick cotton (kirbas), not necessarily leather. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position of the school, which is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; Imam Abu Hanifa reportedly reverted to this opinion. The first condition is that the khuffs be worn after washing the feet, even if the washing is done before completing the entire wudu, provided that the wudu is completed before any nullifier occurs. The author clarifies that the khuff acts as a preventer (mani‘) of hadath reaching the foot, not a remover (rafi‘). Therefore, if one washes his feet, wears khuffs, then completes the rest of wudu before any nullifier, his wudu is sound and he may wipe over the khuffs later. The second condition is that the khuffs must cover the ankles from the sides; seeing the ankles from the top due to a short leg opening does not harm. If the khuff does not cover the ankle due to short length, it can be remedied by sewing thick material to it. The third condition is that continuous walking in them must be possible; hence wiping is not allowed on khuffs made of glass, wood, or iron, as walking in them is not feasible without support. The fourth condition is that each khuff must be free from a hole equal to three of the smallest toes of the foot. There is a difference: some say measure by the fingers of the hand. The relied-upon position is by istihsan, since khuffs normally have small holes; only large holes prevent wiping. The hole must be open enough to see what is beneath; closed holes even of three fingers' size are not considered. These conditions ensure that the khuff serves its purpose of allowing ease in walking while covering the foot in a state of purity.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A footwear that covers the foot up to the ankles, typically made of leather or thick material, worn for walking.
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over the khuffs with wet hands instead of washing the feet in wudu, a concession for ease.
مانع (mani‘): A preventer; the khuff prevents the hadath (ritual impurity) from reaching the foot, so it does not nullify wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wiping over a khuff made of thick cotton (kirbas) that has a hole equal to two small toes?
A) Permissible because the material is thick and the hole is small.
B) Not permissible because the khuff is not leather.
C) Permissible only for travelers.
D) Not permissible because the hole is too large.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is valid only if worn after washing feet (completed wudu before nullifier), cover ankles, allow walking, and have no hole equal to three smallest toes—thick non-leather materials are allowed.
